		<username>Ralph Michael Stein (riglltesobxs@mailinator.com)</username>
		<score>0.7</score>
		<shortDescription>An Unoriginal Caper Comedy But It's Fun (Real Fun)</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>The Coen brothers can be depended on to produce maliciously funny mischief by taking a not particularly original idea and making it work through some very fine acting."The Ladykillers" isn't for everyone - for a start its length will be reduced by two-thirds for ultimate TV viewing when all the "f"-words are excised - there's that many.There aren't too many stereotypes missing in this tale of a master criminal with an assortment of comedic oddballs planning to burglarize and rob a Mississippi River gambling boat's money room. Tom Hanks sparkles as the pseudo-professor with the unpronounceable name of Goldthwait Higgenson Dorr who rents a room from elderly, black mama Marva Munson, played by Irma P. Hall. For her charming portrayal of a gospel-loving, God-fearing widow who won't tolerate any bad language or smoking in her very nice home, Ms. Hall fully earned above-the-title credit.Dorr rents a room and brings in his gang of four. J. K. Simmons, sprung from his shrink role on "Law and Order," is an explosives expert of sorts. Tzi Ma, "The General," is the tactical planner, one of "our" Vietnamese officers now ensconced in the U.S. Ryan Hurst is Lump Hudson, a former football player whose brain was damaged long before he took to the gridiron: the staple idiot in the gang. Lastly is Marlon Wayons as the the inside man, a janitor at the casino, Gawain MacSam. Wayons is sure to win the Oscar next February for Best Actor in a Totally Foulmouthed Role.To complete the picture of a river town on the mighty Mississippi, we have a somnolent sheriff (black) and an equally laid back deputy (white). And, of course, the scene would be unreal without some righteous preaching and foot-stomping singing in a black church.Telling his landlady that he and his friends need her root cellar to practice church music from the Renaissance, they begin tunneling towards the river bank and the coveted millions in anticipated loot.That's enough of the plot which unfolds with few surprises until nearly the end when an identifiably Coen stamp is put on the denouement. Pay particular attention to the antics of Pickles the cat, a superb feline actor with, I suspect, a bright future in movies.Dorr, a nonstop double-talker spouting mellifluous academic argot, is as smooth and as deep as the winter's first sheen of ice. Munson doesn't really know what to make of him at first. Gullible initially, she reveals the steely inside we expect of a caricatured devout churchgoer. Say hallelujah, fellow movie fans."The Ladykillers" is the Coen brothers flip side: "Fargo" is another world. As such it's entertaining because Hanks and Hall are wrapped in their roles.Carefully watching end credits occasionally pays off. Instead of the usual listing for "Legal Counsel," the production's attorney is identified with the label "Serious Matters." :)7/10.</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>doctor_slo</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Good for most movies, average for Coens</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>What I like most about the Coens is their ability to write fantastic dialogue. Even when their characters are terse and laconic, which makes lines like "Where's pancakes house?" memorable, their ability to fill the mouths of actors with some of the best words spoken in movies keeps their mavens returning to their features again and again.I was amazed at their ability to fill Tom Hanks' mouth with flowery pedantries, Marlon Wayans' mouth with inner city Ebonics, and Irma Hall's mouth with sensible southern plain-speak. But the problem I had was that these all seemed to be exercises in writing. It reminded me of the disclaimer Mark Twain wrote at the beginning of Huckleberry Finn where he describes the dialects he attempted to capture in the book. He wanted to disabuse his reader of the notion that "all these characters were trying to talk alike and not succeeding."I could see the Coens exercising their writing chops, and feeling the muscle of their dialogue, skimped on some character development. Don't get me wrong. I would rather watch a poorer Coen effort than watch a dozen pieces of drek offered as movies today. Most of this film delighted me whereas the parts I found wanting I would have gladly overlooked in any Michael Bay film.So if I were to rate this against movies in general **** 1/2 out of five. Against other Coen works ** 1/2. If you're not a Coen fan, you'll be delighted (or appalled if the foul language gets to you), and if you are a Coen fan, you'll be mildly amused.</fullReview>

		<username>sports-8</username>
		<score>-1.0</score>
		<shortDescription>Coen brothers, Hanks make great combination</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Dark, dark, dark. Dark and funny. That's what one can expect from just about any Coen brothers (Joel and Ethan) film. From "Blood Simple" to "Raising Arizona" to "Barton Fink" to "The Hudsucker Proxy" to "Fargo" to "The Big Lebowski" to "O' Brother, Where Art Thou?" to their newest release, "The Ladykillers." The film is a remake of the 1955 classic starring Alec Guiness, Peter Sellers and Katie Johnson. In this version, Tom Hanks portrays a Southern professor who, along with a ragtag gang of reprobates, plans to rob a riverboat casino in Tennessee. To accomplish this, Prof. G.H. Dorr (Hanks) rents a room in the house of a sweet, elderly black lady, Marva Munson (Irma P. Hall), who seems unaware enough, until a series of mishaps plague the group. Suffering these indignities include Gawain McSam (a hilarious Marlon Wayans), martial arts expert, The General (Tzi Ma), explosives man, Garth Pancake (J.K. Simmons, "Law &amp; Order: SVU") and hulky Lump Hudson (Ryan Hurst, "Remember The Titans"). Dorr seems to have the perfect plan to execute the heist, simply rent the room, tell Marva they are practicing Medevial musical instruments in her root cellar, dig a short tunnel to the casino's vault and use McSam, a riverboat janitor, as the inside man. Unfortunately, things begin to go south almost immediately.McSam makes rude comments about a customer's posterior and is fired. In a hilarious scene featuring his boss, Ferdinand Gudge (Stephen Root, "News Radio"), he is forced to apologize with chocolates and $100. Pancake, who suffers from severe attacks of Irritable Bowel Syndrome, also brings his girlfriend, Mountain Girl (Diane Delano), into the plan, unbeknownst to any of the others. This results in a riotous running fight between him and McSam. As for Hudson, he is as big and stupid as a person can be, and makes one wonder why he would have been part of such an intricate plan in the first place. Despite these setbacks, as well as a mutilating explosion and near discovery of their plan on several occasions, the gang somehow manages to pull off the robbery and net over $1.6 million. They are finally found out by Marva, however, who gives Prof. Dorr the option of returning the cash to its rightful owners and coming with her to church - or going to jail for the crime. This new development necessitates the plan to off her, but no one wants to do the dirty job. Support is added by comedian George Wallace and John McDonald as disbelieving law enforcement officers. Hanks is in top form, with slow southern drawl interrupted with fits of insanane giggling, but it's Hall who steals this film with a great sincere performance. Don't be surprised if her name appears as a Best Supporting Actress next year. You read it here first. "The Ladykillers" opened on Friday, March 19, but beware of the many F-bombs, causing it's 'R' rating</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>Generally misbegotten remake, with foul language and cartoonish characters...</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>Joel and Ethan Coen's remake of the well-regarded 1955 British comedy starring Alec Guinness begins wonderfully, with righteous-living Irma P. Hall renting out her spare room to 'professor' Tom Hanks (with funny teeth and Southern drawl). But as soon as Hanks' motley team of casino-robbing cohorts come into the picture, the jokes get stuck in a boring rut, undermined by nasty talk, stereotyping and hyped-up action. The old-fashioned trimmings (such as a lengthy sequence with Hall attending church, presided over by a flamboyant minister and gospel choir) do not jell with the low-ball humor permeating the majority of the film; and, while it's a great-looking movie with a handsome production design, it isn't particularly well-acted or convincing on its comedic terms. A misfire. *1/2 from ****</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>An odd, odd comedy- I was fascinated by how it wouldn't always work, in a sense...</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>While the Coen brothers may not seem as tuned into quality over quantity in their latest Hollywood efforts, the thing that keeps me interested is that they don't lose their voice along the way. It would be a shame if the Coens perhaps continued on the path they are taking, which is that of star vehicles, but whatever they've done in their career hasn't been messed around with by the men upstairs. In fact, I would imagine that there were very few notes to the Coens about things like content and style. How can you give these guys notes, even when they seem like they're making a comedy for themselves? The Ladykillers is a silly, foul-mouthed little remake exercise that surely isn't as successful as their best (Fargo, Blood Simple, O' Brother, Where Art Thou), however isn't as sad as their worst (Intolerable Cruelty, which wasn't a failure but just at the average mark for them). There's a curious, assured quality in their direction, as their cinematographer Roger Deakins offers up some memorable images in this somewhat picturesque, Southern landscape. Tom Hanks, as the Professor G.H. Dorr, is hard not to look at even when some of his jokes fall on deaf ears in the audience. His performance, believe it or not, is sort of mesmerizing, in his speech, attire, even in how he recites EA Poe. And the supporting cast isn't bad either, with JK Simmons and Marlon Wayans not as bad as they could've been. Irma P. Hall, as the heart of the film, was deserved of her win at Cannes.I guess the main flaw in the film, if their is one to point out, is that the Coens try to combine types of humor that may not quite work for them (flatulence jokes do work, but it's tricky to pull them off unless you're going for full-on, no-holds-barred stupid), and when their film takes some dark turns, they're dark in the blackest comedic sense (i.e. the third act). The plot itself becomes a little more predictable as the thieves' tale unfolds. And as for the style, while still in control, goes off the wall more times than desired. In other words, The Ladykillers is maybe a mess, yet the kind of mess that should appeal to the Coens' die-hard fan base, and to those who like seeing Hanks do something, err, different. And don't forget the catchy gospel soundtrack, which garners as much toe-tapping as O' Brother. B-</fullReview>
	</review>

		<username>The_Void</username>
		<score>0.7</score>
		<shortDescription>Very decent remake</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>The train got replaced by a boat, London with the American Deep south, Alec Guinness with Tom Hanks, The parrot by a cat, the bank with a Casino and the kind, feeble old lady with a more astute black woman; which somewhat misses the point of the original. In the original film, the majority of the comedy element came from the way that the old woman had no idea what was going on in her home; because of her being old and naive, we were able to believe that she wasn't suspicious and had no idea. However, in the remake it's not so believable that this woman would not know what's going on; some attempt is made to establish her as a kindly old lady that knows no bad from her distaste for "hippety Hop" music and the fact that she goes to church, but she doesn't capture the feeble and naiveness of her predecessor, which in my opinion harms the comedy element of which the original did so well.That aside, this movie does have a great deal of good things going for it; most notably a very hammy, eccentric and hilarious performance from Tom Hanks. Alec Guinness is one of the finest actors of all time, and following in his footsteps is no easy feat; but Tom Hanks really proves himself as an actor here by following Guinness remarkably well. From the moment he is introduced, in a very similar if less sinister sequence to that shown in the original masterpiece, we can see that Hanks has got the atmosphere of his character just right. The only slight annoyance of his character is the little laugh he does now and again between lines...it would have served the movie better if that was left out in my opinion, but it isn't even nearly enough to scotch my all time favourite Tom Hanks performance.Unlike the original, and one thing that I think the remake does better is that the gang of small-time, hapless, crooks is fleshed out a little. In the original, the characters turned up the house, without anything made clear about their characters, whereas this time each one is given a little introduction; which aside from being hilarious, also gives the audience a feel for each one of them, which really helps the movie. The gang features two really notable standout performances from J.K. Simmons (the unsung star of Spider-Man) and Marlon Wayans, who does a surprisingly good job as Gawain MacSam (you've got to love the character names!). These two add a third dimension of comedy to an already wonderful comedy thriller.The original was a very dark comedy, and so is this film, although this one is certainly a lot lighter. It doesn't take advantage of the absurdness that the original had (the lop-sided house), and it doesn't get dark till very late on either; and that is something which could have been better. However, cinema audiences have come to expect a lot from Coen brothers films, and this one, despite being a remake, does not disappoint. As an Englishman, and a fan of the original; I say the Coens almost did it justice.</fullReview>
	</review>

This film actually is Hanks' more successful return to the genre of comedy, since `Catch me if you can' was a real bore. Hanks stars as the leader of an amateurish brat pack that plans on robbing the local casino. Via the cellar of a seemly harmless old lady, they're digging a tunnel that ends in the casino's safe. The Ladykillers contains a few downright brilliant comedy-sequences (like when every gang-member is introduced separately) and an irresistible atmosphere. This is comedy how I like to see it. No tasteless images of sexually obsessed teenagers, but smart, comical situations and extravagant characters. Aside from the flawless performance by Tom Hanks, all the other acting performances are remarkable as well. J.K Simmons is great and proves he can handle more than just small, supportive roles. Heck, even Marlon Wayans' performance is decent as long his directed by professionals like the Coens. This film certainly isn't my favorite Coen film (films like `Blood Simple', `Fargo', `Raising Arizona' or `The Big Lebowski' are almost impossible to top) but it certainly ranks among the best films I've seen this year. Unfortunately, I haven't had the chance to see the original 1955 title on which this one is based. I want to, since it stars one of my all-time favorite actors, Herbert Lom.</fullReview>

		<shortDescription>The Ladykillers</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>The original 1955 film starring Sir Alec Guinness, Peter Sellers and Herbert Lom is a true comedy classic, so many questioned why it was going to be remade, especially by directing brothers Joel and Ethan Coen (Fargo, No Country for Old Men, True Grit). Basically in Saucier, Mississippi lives elderly, God-fearing and uptight widow Marva Munson (Irma P. Hall) who gets an unexpected visit from the eccentric Southern Professor G.H. Dorr (Tom Hanks). He is interested in letting the room she has for rent, which she accepts, and he is also to be joined by his "band", casino worker Gawain MacSam (Marlon Wayans), explosives expert Garth Pancake (Spider-Man's J.K. Simmons), tunnelling expert The General (Tzi Ma) and thick but thuggish Lump Hudson (Ryan Hurst). Of course they are not musicians, but criminals planning to tunnel their way through the dried earth to the casino vault not far from Mrs. Munson's house, and all their individual skills will come in handy. They manage to reach the vault, and successfully remove the millions of dollars inside, but it is when the tunnel needs to be blown up that things go wrong, because Mrs. Munson comes home early, hears the explosion, and the money is flying everywhere. The Professor tries to lie his way out of it and convince her that they have taken it for good intentions, but of course she doesn't buy it and wants them to return the money, or she will report to the police. The criminals know that the only way they can keep the money is to kill the old woman, and they draw straws to see who is going to do it, and even when Gawain gets it, he refuses. This creates an argument, ending with with Gawain accidentally shooting himself, and while dispensing of the body Pancake sees the opportunity to get away with the money with his wife Mountain Girl (Diane Delano). Of course they end up being killed as well, and the straws are drawn again, The General is the loser, and when it looks like he will kill Mrs. Munson he ends up falling down the stairs. Finally it is just Lump and The Professor left, Lump doesn't want him to kill the old lady and ends up shooting himself, while The Professor dies having a statue head fall on him, hanging by his cloak, and falling into the trash boat below. In the end, all the money has been left behind, and when Mrs. Munson tries to return the money to the police, they think she is crazy and jokingly say that she should do whatever she wants with the money. Also starring George Wallace as Sheriff Wyner, John McConnell as Deputy Sheriff and Heroes' Greg Grunberg as TV Commercial Director. Hanks is reasonable as the Professor with the big teeth and Southern accent, but he's no Sir Alec Guinness, same goes for Hall as the old lady, she isn't lovably kind and innocent like the upstaging and BAFTA winning Katie Johnson, and the supporting cast have their small moments as well. The scripting has its moments of wittiness, and it feels almost as amusingly sinister and quirky like the original, but you know it's not as good and never could be, it is alright black comedy. Okay!</fullReview>

		<date>2005-03-30</date>
		<username>Roland E. Zwick (magneteach@aol.com)</username>
		<score>0.6</score>
		<shortDescription>barely passable remake of a comic masterpiece</shortDescription>
		<fullReview>In the interest of full disclosure, let me state right up front that the 1955 Ealing Brothers classic, "The Ladykillers," ranks as one of my all-time favorite comedies. A masterpiece of tone, the film, written by William Rose and directed by Alexander MacKendrick, is not only a sweet and gentle tale full of subtle wit and endearing whimsy but also a murderously funny black comedy centered on homicide and death. A group of thieves, planning a heist, rent a room from an old lady who lives in her own insulated world of tea parties and Victorian Era innocence. Pretending to be musicians, the crooks use both her and her establishment as convenient blinds for their nefarious activities. The great fun of the film lies in watching the bad guys get their richly deserved comeuppance in the end, while the sweet little old lady escapes unscathed and unharmed.Now a new set of brothers - the Coen Brothers - have decided to take a whack at the same material, but their attempt at modernizing this priceless comic gem falls flat for a number of reasons. First and foremost, the remake systematically violates the spirit and tone of the original. The genius in the '50's film derived from the juxtaposition between the evil motives of the criminals and the utter innocence of the sweet and befuddled old lady. In this new version, which has been awkwardly transplanted from cool, foggy London to steaming Mississippi, the old woman has been conceived as a far more mouthy, far more worldly individual, thereby undercutting the original's comic tension right off the bat. It also doesn't help that the overall tone - as befits the current times - is far more crude, crass and vulgar, whereas it was the extreme gentility of the lady's insulated world that made the original comedy work so well.Tom Hanks has taken over the role, originally filled by the inimitable Alec Guinness, of the group's leader and mastermind, here called Professor G. H. Dorr. Hanks portrays him as a silver-tongued, poetry-spouting, white-suited gentleman (think a young Colonel Sanders), an anachronistic throwback to the days of the pre-bellum genteel South. In fact, there is more of a comic contrast between Dorr and the men he is working with than there is between the crooks and their hostess. Yet, it is a comic tension that pays off less well than the original. The characters all too often turn into caricatures, and the comedy is frequently broader and less subtle in tone than it needs to be. Another problem is that, in the original version, the men actually use Mrs. Wilberforce to innocently tote their ill-gotten gains for them. This clever little way of implicating the little old lady in the crime has been inexplicably dropped from this version.Having said all that, however, I must admit that there are some genuinely amusing moments in the film, particularly in the second half, and the material itself is so ingenious and sturdy that it would be hard for any filmmakers - let alone those of the caliber of the Coen Brothers - to fail utterly in the endeavor. Hanks gives a clever, winning performance as Dorr, despite the fact that filling Guinness' shoes is a tall order for any actor, no matter how talented and skillful. Irma P. Hall does a nice job as Mrs. Munson, even if her performance lacks the subtle shading of Katie Johnson's original.If "The Ladykillers" weren't toiling in the shadow of its great predecessor, it might seem like a clever, offbeat little comedy, and perhaps that's the way it does appear to those unfamiliar with the original. But, as a die-hard fan, I suggest you search out the real thing instead.</fullReview>
	</review>
